text:
This is 3 stars if you make it as written, which I did.  But it was very hard to spread, even on a 9 x 13 sheet cake. I couldn't even imagine trying to frost a layer cake with it like this.  So, I decided to chalk that cake up to experience and made another.  This time I used a heaping cup of Jif peanut butter (probably around 1 1/4 cups), 1 1/2 cups of powdered sugar and 3 T of heavy cream.  I beat the room temperature butter and the room temperature peanut butter for several minutes until I could not see any butter at all in the mixture and it seemed very creamy.  Then I gradually added the powdered sugar and when it was well-blended, I added the 3 T of heavy cream and then put it on #6 on my KitchenAid mixer and let it go for 3-4 minutes.  This time it was MUCH easier to spread and tastes great!!

Very easy and nice. However, in order to get a good consistency, all ingredients should be at room temperature. If they get too grainy and hard after u added in 3 tablespoons milk, stop adding. Instead, put ur bowl into microwave on high for 30 sec, take out and stir. This will solve the problem. Great frosting. Very peanut buttery!

text:
This frosting is amazing--it balances flavor against sweetness well, and the texture was perfect:  creamy, fluffy, not oily at all.  I followed the recipe EXACTLY as written, no alterations necessary.  I made sure my butter was softened (not just room temperature) and I used Jiff's Creamy PB with No Added Sugar;  the two whipped together beautifully in about a minute (and I just own a bottom-barrel Black & Decker hand-held mixer);  then I added the powdered sugar a half-cup at a time, whipping as I went;  I made sure to add in 1 Tbl milk between each sugar-addition so that I could judge moisture-spreadability ratio.  It kept wonderfully fluffy and spreadable for the hour and a half that I used it, then put the remainder in the fridge.  It does harden in the fridge, but gently microwaving it with a tablespoon or two or milk and then stirring returns it to its original malleability.  I liked this recipe so well, I made an additional batch substituting Nutella for the peanut butter--it tasted incredible!

text:
I also give 3 stars for this recipe "as is." I took another reviewer's advice and used 1.25 cups peanut butter (Jif), 1.5 cups of powdered sugar; however, I didn't have cream at home, so I used 2 tbsp 2% milk (lactose free), and it turned out beautifully! I creamed the peanut butter & room temperature butter then added the powdered sugar 1/2 cup at a time, and adding the milk 1 tbsp at at time at the end. It spread very easily on my 9x13 devil's food cake and tasted delicious! Made this way, my family and I give it 5 stars!!!

I see how this could be an awesome frosting...and its my fault it did not turn out right. I did not have any butter left in the house, so I used country crock butter spread instead. DO NOT USE IT. It is in no way a butter substitute other than to use on bread. I knew this from past experience, but i decided to try again anyways since its a frosting not a cookie recipie (country crock does not work for cookies either) what I ended up with was a chunky, liquidy peanut butter spread. Not wanting to just put it in the all in the trash, I put the glob in the fridge and that helped a bit. The flavor was there-the frosting consistency was not. So this a warning to those of you like me who try to just use whats in the house-don't. I will be trying this again with butter and I'm sure it will be just as great as the other reviews say.

This is the easiest frosting recipe I have ever made and it is definitely one of the tastiest!! One note is that I did not have to use all 3 tablespoons of milk and only used 1 as the frosting did not get too thick for my liking.  

I was a true cynic about using peanut butter in anything but a sandwich or on a cracker.  I offered to make a birthday cake for a friend and she said she loved peanut butter and chocolate - so I had a task!  I made this icing three days ahead of time expecting some sort of disaster and recovery effort, but it is wonderful!!  I could not stop test-tasting it! Now I have a wonderful alternative to regular buttercream!

text:
Wow!  I am IN LOVE!  Since I am a peanut butter freak and love all things peanut butter, I went in search of a peanut butter frosting recipe to frost my delicious Texas Sheath Cake I was going to bake.  I didn't want an icing kind of thing, I wanted a nice fluffy, totally peanut butter tasting frosting and I am so glad I found this!  I looked at several different recipes before deciding this one looked more to my liking.  I am not a fan of sickening sweet frosting and usually no matter what recipe I use, I never put in the full amount of powdered sugar.  Even with this recipe, I didn't use the full amount.  But here's the kicker.  I only had Laura Scudder's Natural Peanut Butter, the kind you have to stir because it separates.  Not caring if it came out more dense, I went ahead and used it and my frosting came out fluffy and delicious!  I'm wondering if the people who complained about the frosting being greasy only mixed the ingredients together.  I used my old hand held beaters and put it on high and whipped the heck out of.  As soon as I poured the cream into it (I used cream instead of milk), it started to look more fluffy.  I rough guessed at the amount of cream I put in and then started adding the powdered sugar.  It just beat up so nicely and as soon as it was sweet enough for me, I stopped whipping it and frosted my cake.  I thoroughly enjoyed licking off the beaters and cleaning out the remnants of the bowl.  Addicting, delicious and I'll be making this forever more.

text:
My best friend does not like buttercream - but adores peanut butter.  I found this for his birthday many years ago and it was a hit! 
This icing has been a HUGE hit at my office: I am the "cupcake lady" and this icing is my top request, especially with chocolate-fudge cupcakes. 
Fluffy, wonderful flavor, not overly sweet.  
I owned a cake business many years ago - so I will tell you it is a bit thick to spread by hand, you really need to use a pastry bag with a large tip.  If you really want to spread it, add another Tablespoon of milk. 
I *only* use whole milk in my icings because the flavor and texture whole milk adds does make a difference.  
Also, my butter is always room temperature, as is the milk. 
The temperature of the dairy will impact the creaminess and pipe-ability/spread-ability of the icing.

text:
Loved loved loved it!  The key is to not overbeat this, and to use a good peanut butter (like creamy Jiff).  I beat the butter and peanut butter until really creamy - probably a good 3-4 minutes in my Kitchen Aid with the paddle attachment.  Add the sugar and a little milk at a time, mixing well until nice and creamy.  If you over beat, it will start to separate and look "chunky".  Stop when it's still creamy, and you won't be disappointed.  I used this to top the Brownie Batter + Cupcake recipe (also from this site), and the combination of the two was out of this world!  Can't wait to use this one on plain brownies in the future!  Thanks for the recipe!

text:
I have no clue how people are not getting perfectly fluffy frosting if directions are followed to a T.   I did not change a thing and i am so happy with the results.  Do NOT use margarine.  Margarine does not have the same consistency of butter and your frosting will not be as fluffy.  Also it says to add milk AS NEEDED.  I only needed about a tablespoon of the milk.  If you use real  butter and milk only as needed instead of the full 3T, than your frosting should turn out well. I made the too much chocolate cake from this site,  with homeade chocolate frosting and bordered the cake and wrote all over the cake with this PB frosting. It was the perfect combo.

text:
I think the difference between a broken greasy blob and a wonderfully fluffy frosting is twofold. 1) The proper ingredients at just the right temperature, and 2) a stand mixer vs a hand-held mixer. I used a stand mixer, Jif Natural peanut butter, and organic butter that was room temp. For a few brief seconds I saw 'fluffy' and then it turned 'lumpy and greasy'. I used it anyway as the filling for my cakes, since it tasted fine. Then I took the leftovers and stiffened them up by adding several tablespoons of cocoa powder and a bit of heavy cream. 

I would suggest using the cream instead of milk, since the water content of milk will tend to increase the risk of breaking. Likewise I would recommend using a handheld mixer to make the 'fluffy' stage a little easier to spot before it disappears. 

The cocoa-stiffened leftovers became writing icing, and I ended up frosting the cake with a chocolate buttercream. It all worked out in the end, but I did want to suggest not using the stand mixer for other folks who try this in the future. 

Personally, I found the peanut butter flavor a bit weaker than I wanted. The recipe definitely needs some salt to get back that 'reese's cup' type flavor. I probably won't end up using this one again because of that. Maybe a stronger flavored peanut butter would help.

text:
I made this recipe written as-is the first time around.  It had great flavor but still not the texture/consistency I was looking for.  I needed something that wasn't overly sweet but that would still pipe rosettes beautifully around a bundt cake.  So the second time around I needed to double the recipe.  Here's what I used:  One 16-oz. jar of PB, 3 C. sifted powdered sugar, 9 Tbsp. of half and half, 1 stick of butter (1/2 C.), and 1/2 C. of shortening.  I first creamed the butter since it was firmer than the other ingredients.  Once the PB started to increase in volume and turn lighter, I slowly added in the shortening and PB.  Then, one half cup at a time, I slowly mixed in the sugar and a few Tbsp. of liquid at a time.  I wanted to try and get this smooth, but at the end it still has a lot of air in it, which is okay since I won't be smoothing it over a large area.  So I basically had to decrease the sugar amount by 1/2 C. and increase liquid by 2 Tbsp. if looking at the original recipe.  I also added in a cap of vanilla extract.  The best way to make an actual frosting is to use a standard butter cream recipe and just simply add in a 1/2 C. of PB.  The PB flavor isn't as strong and the frosting is sweet, but it will actually be a frosting you can smooth out and decorate.  But the flavor of this recipe is much better.  I would def. use it as a filling or frosting for chocolate cupcakes!

text:
I'm giving this recipe a 3 star due to the directions, because to me they seem a little off. I made this last night exactly how the recipe states and it was a disaster. After gradually adding the last cup of confectioners sugar the "frosting" seized, big time. After reading others suggestions I gave it another try today. I used the exact measurements of all ingredients, except I added the confectioners sugar about one tablespoon at a time. Once I got through the first cup of sugar I added the first tablespoon of milk. Once the last cup of sugar was in I added the other two tablespoons of milk. The frosting was too thick for my liking so I added about three more tablespoons of milk. Finally!! Iced my cake and now ready to eat. This frosting isn't overpowered by peanut butter, nor is it too sweet. I will admit, however, that it is a little difficult to ice the cake with this frosting. Overall, it's an ok recipe. I will use again if I don't find another that I like.

This is fabulous! I used it to frost heart shaped brownies for my husband for Valentine's day, and it made a LOT. It was thick, but all you have to do is add a touch of milk and keep mixing until it's the consistency that you want. I had so much I also put it on top of Chocolate Mousse that I made, and still have some left over. I would suggest don't add any milk until it gets too thick to mix, and then add a tiny bit at a time until it's just right for you. I highly recommend it!

text:
Absolutely perfect! This was my first attempt ever at making frosting and I was so nervous about how it would turn out but you really can't go wrong with this recipe. I had marinated a German chocolate cake overnight in sweetened condensed milk and I didn't want the frosting to be too overwhelmingly sweet so the only change I made to this recipe was to cut the sugar in half. I added toffee bits and a caramel drizzle to top off the cake and ended up with the perfect marriage of sweet and salty flavors. The frosting was so fluffy and easy to spread and even after sitting outside in the heat all night at a cookout, the cake still looked amazing. I had no problems whatsoever with greasiness, separation, or texture. Everything whipped up nicely with my little Cuisinart hand mixer and the frosting had a lovely creamy consistency along with a beautiful presentation. Everyone raved about how delicious the cake was and several people even asked for the frosting recipe. I will most definitely use this delicious recipe again and again!

text:
Excellent frosting. Tastes like a creamy Reese's peanut butter cup filling.

I was concerned about consistency. I made sure to beat butter & peanut butter well, adding 1-teaspoon vanilla. Then, added only 1/2-cup powdered sugar at a time, alternating with 1-tablespoon milk, until I achieve the desired consistency.

The thickness of frosting will change with humidity levels in the air, and the brand powdered sugar you use. By adding only part of the sugar at a time, you eliminate any problems with consistency.
Bon Appetit!

text:
Im fairly good at cooking, what a mess this recipe was. It separated and nothing I did could get it to re-emulsify. I ended up with a thick blob of fudge like stuff and the milk and oil separated out. I read on-line and to try and get it to come back together they recommended adding a block of unsweetened melted chocolate as an emulsifier. It didnt work - now I had a blob of peanut butter chocolate. I didnt want this all to go to waste so I decided to try and heat it up and melt it all together.  I put the blob over low heat and started mixing. Once it started to get melty, I added the oil and liquids that had curdled out and I kept mixing. I ended up with a thick glaze like chocolate peanut butter icing. I iced the cupcakes and everyone loved them. My son who took them to a graduation party reported that the kids thought they tasted like Girl Scout Tagalong cookies. The 2 star review is because the original recipe didnt work for me.

text:
Made this for my dad b/c he mentioned wanting some with chocolate cake (a few months ago) and then I found this recipe.

I did make a few changes.  I ended up using less sugar (1/3 to 1/2 less) than it called for.  And then I added more peanut butter, and then some 1/3 to 1/2 package of plain cream cheese (first to cut more of the sweetness down, and the cream cheese b/c I said "why not?").  And then I might have used more milk.  I just splashed the milk in from time to time.  I would rate it 5 stars with using less sugar (and my other tweaks didn't hurt).

But it stayed really soft and fluffy for me.  In fact, my dad thought it was too fluffy--he thought it would be thicker.

It stiffened up in the refrigerator, but then got back to smooth and fluffy when it sat out a bit.

Start out with a small amount of sugar and taste as you go.  I bet you won't use all 2 cups.  If you have a magic bullet to make the powdered sugar--even better!

It must be REALLY GOOD b/c my dad ate four slices of chocolate cake with my frosting in less than 2 hours!

AND IT'S REALLY GOOD AS THE DIP FOR TART APPLE SLICES--LIKE McINTOSH APPLES!

I keep coming back to this recipe as my base (and to remember it) and then add my little tweaks.

text:
My mother made this icing for ALL of our birthdays so we had it at least 6 times per year...always on a layered Devil's Food cake.   I always use Jif and because its on Devil's Food, I only use 1/2 cup PB (I always use same amount of butter as peanut butter).  If I were icing a yellow cake, and wanted more of a PB flavor, I'd use more PB but I make a Devil's Food cake that is not very sweet but very flavorful so I just use 1/2 cup.  Turns out perfectly every time.  I really think the key is to not use fancy PB...use Jif and real butter not margarine.  Very fluffy and spreadable.

text:
I've made this recipe several times, and it's always come out great for me. It's fluffy and easy to spread. Just always make sure you don't overboard with the milk. Like the recipe says, go one tablespoon at a time so you don't get too much liquid in there. Sometimes I needed all three, but sometimes I only needed two. I don't know why other people's came out "like concrete," because this is much easier to spread for me than the store bought frostings, which are sugary and over-powering. Great peanut butter flavor. Will definitely be using this as a go-to.

text:
This recipe was wonderful the first time I made it!  Best frosting I've ever tasted and it made so much!  Second time, I was not able to spread it at all.  The only difference was that I beat it the extra 3 minutes at the end which made it unspreadable.  The first time I made it I didn't even see that step and as soon as I mixed the powdered sugar in with the already creamed butter and peanut butter, I used it to frost the cake.  And the taste was marvelous!  So good I wanted to make it again which I did and this time I saw the beat for 3 minutes and did that.  It turned what was a beautiful creamy frosting into a peanut butter fudgey type mess.  I almost cried since it was my birthday cake.  But I plopped it on and we ate it anyway.  Great recipe but I recommend do not beat it the extra 3 minutes at the end.  It might turn out for some but since I made it both ways I just wanted to offer my suggestion to make it spreadable.

I made this icing as suggested and it turned out great.  It wasn't hard to spread on the cake at all.  I creamed the peanut butter and butter first for 2 mins and then I added the powdered sugar.  As soon as I added the powdered sugar it became dry, but as soon as I added the milk it became smooth again.  I tried spreading the icing on the cake with my spreader but ended up using my hands because the mixture wasn't staying on, but if I molded the icing on it stayed in place.  It tasted amazing!!  I used Natural PB Jif since I only eat natural PB.  Sometimes it is better to use original PB, but I opted to try the Natural and it worked perfectly.  I used this icining on the Too Much Chocolate Cake Recipe also found in All Recipes and garnished with crushed peanut butter cups.  Was an amazing cake!!!  My new favorite!!

text:
When making this icing, I revised the recipe for more of a butter-cream consistency:Blend into the peanut butter and softened butter- 2 Tablespoons(TBS) vegetable shortening and 1 tsp vanilla, mix until creamy consistency. I added 1 more TBS of butter to make it more creamier. Continue to add milk 1 TBS and 1 cup of powdered sugar at a time. You will end up using only 2 TBS milk and 2 cups of powdered sugar. By the way, no need to sift the sugar. My family and friends devoured my cake and loved the chocolate-peanut butter combination. This should fix any issues with spreading the icing.

Well, I just halved the recipe to frost an 8 x 8 inch pan of brownies. I even ballparked the peanut butter and butter, did not pack the sugar, and used 2 tbsp of milk. I pretty much followed the directions, beating on medium with an electric mixer, at every step. I added a little more sugar at the end to make it a little stiffer, and well, I can't see the problem the one reviewer who gave it 3 stars had. My daughter gave this 3 thumbs up. I haven't frosted the brownies yet, but it has great enough flavor for this house. Instant dress up for my DH brownies. Massive pms fix.

This recipe was super easy and tasty. I made it for the topping on my mother's birthday brownies. She LOVED it way more than her own PB frosting recipe - which is really saying something! 

The only complaint I have is that it was a little too sweet for my taste. I would scale back the powdered sugar to 1 1/2 cups.

All in all, GREAT recipe!

The first time I made this recipe, it didn't go so well - i use extra creamy peanut butter, and the icing refused to get fluffy, and was smooth and creamy like regular peanut butter.  It still tasted good though, so I decided to re-try the recipe.

I made a full recipe, and followed it exactly with the exception that I substituted the milk for cream, and I only used about half. city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
Perfect as is. Extremely fluffy and very easy to spread. I don't understand how anyone can find it too stiff. I beat the heck out of SOFT butter and room temp low sugar PB with the whisk attachment until it's fluffy and the add the POWDERED sugar 1/2 cup at a time. After the first cup, add a TBL of milk or cream.  Keep adding powdered sugar and cream until it reaches the consistency you want. You can add/subtract PB and sugar according to your taste. No way this can fail IF you follow the recipe as written. If you substitute margarine then don't expect it to turn out well and certainly don't rate it based on your mistake! And don't even think about trying granulated sugar! You'll have gritty frosting for sure.

text:
Made this for a 9" chocolate layer cake.  As I was mixing (and taste testing), I noticed two things: you would need more milk to deal with 2 cups of sugar and that 2 cups of sugar would be almost unbearably sweet.  I ended up using 1/2 cup butter, 1 cup pb, 3+ tbs milk and less than 1 1/3 cup of sugar.  With these changes it was still peanut buttery and not over the top sugary.

text:
I used Jif PB and real butter. It wasn't oily at all for me, but I did use a stand mixer instead of a hand mixer. Maybe that's the difference some people are having with the recipe that's causing the oiliness. Also, the butter should be softened, but not melting. Too warm butter would cause oiliness for sure.   It was perfectly spreadable for me. If it looks too stiff in the bowl, just add a little more milk.  The only change I made was adding a little vanilla extract. The only mistake I made was not doubling the recipe!! Great recipe! Thanks!

text:
A co-worker loves the peanut butter frosted brownies (topped with chopped nuts and a chocolate swirl) made by the the Awrey Bakery Company located here in Livonia, and she wanted to know if I could duplicate the recipe. Of course I went right to Allrecipes.  I found this recipe and BINGO - the perfect Peanut Butter Frosting.  I made as directed and had no problems although I admit it is a little difficult to spread. Using a 9 x 13 pan, I found that if you put a lot of some dollops across the entire brownies (works even better if they are still barely warm) and then use a metal spatula and spread in long strokes.  I then melt chocolate with a small amount of shortening, put it in a piping bag, and drizzle the chocolate back and forth in one direction, then the other and (optional) chopped nuts. Then I cover with foil and refrigerate before serving. WOW!  This has been a hit to every party I have taken it to. Haven't tried in on cake, but great on moist brownies!

text:
Everyone loved this on the brownies I made. I took the advice of another reviewer and used less confectioners sugar. I think that was my only mistake. I creamed the peanut butter and "margarine" (was all I had) really good then added the confectioners' sugar a little at a time, constantly mixing. Also, added the milk (skim - all I had) a little at a time until I got the consistency I wanted - all the while mixing. Used more than 3 tbsp. of milk, but the recipe says as needed and I was using skim. Turned out great for me although I admit I was concerned until I started adding the milk. It was enough for 2 - 8" pans of brownies. Follow the recipe and it will turn out great for you too.

This was really good.  I made the recipe exactly as written and it came out perfectly.  Today was my husband's birthday and he wanted brownie cupcakes with peanut butter frosting. text:
The perfect balance of peanut buttery sweetness! I had to fiddle with the recipe a little, as I had no confectioners sugar and knew better than to just substitute white and end up with the grittiest frosting this side of the Mississippi, so I heated the milk in the microwave and dissolved the sugar into it, halving it to 1 cup because white sugar is more potent. It all came together well, but had to be refrigerated before spreading because the heated milk made it quite runny. It set up nicely, though, and a quick fork-whip perked it right up to the perfect frosting texture, in my opinion. Smooth and easily spreadable (and it even got a little pleasantly gooey [but not runny] on my still-warm cake and made it feel very wonderfully decadent). I just can't give 5 stars because I diverted from the original recipe.

text:
I did not make this as written but instead used less sugar and more milk so as to make syrup for Banana Pancakes I from this site. It was so good! I think if I hadn't added milk, it would have set up beautifully for frosting, so I'm giving this frosting a 5 for flavor even though I didn't use it as frosting :) EDIT: Update! Made it again, as frosting. It worked beautifully but you do have to be careful with the wet/dry ratio and adjust. Be flexible. Don't just dump the ingredients in your Kitchenaid all at once and then call the recipe a failure--add them gradually the way the recipe recommends. Humidity and brand of peanut butter DO affect how much liquid or sugar this recipe will need!

text:
My daughter and I tasted the Barefoot Contessa chocolate cupcakes with peanut butter frosting and almost bought the mix because we liked it so much. Looking at the price, however, we decided to try our luck at home.  We didn't like this frosting as much as in the mix, but it was good.  I think that the difference was the Contessa's was more creamy than fluffy and had more of a peanut butter flavor.  The chocolate/ peanut butter combo is a winner, however, so I will make this again and adjust the amount of peanut butter to taste.

text:
I found that the trick to get spreadable icing was to gradually add more cream when the mixture starts to split. With my mixer beating fast, i would add a small drizzle (like 1/2 tsp at a time) until it was loose again. With this process, i was able to turn this from yummy paste to properly whipped icing for a layer cake. 

It does take patience! My first attempt was like paste. if this happens to you - add a bit of dairy and whip more

text:
This is really good, as long as you do it correctly. Whip softened butter until fluffy, then beat in the peanut butter until fluffy again, then add the powdered sugar until your desired sweetness/consistency. I omitted the milk because I wanted a stiff consistency for piping. I also used unsalted butter, but then did add about 1/2 tsp of sea salt to balance the sweetness. Really delicious, fluffy, not greasy, and not too sweet.

text:
I have made this a few times now with mixed results.  Flavor is great but texture was inconsistent.  It didn't work when I tried to beat it in the food processor: it was pasty and it separated.  It worked great when I put real softened butter, PB, and confectioners sugar in a bowl, beat that briefly with a hand held mixer, then added the milk to thin it out.  I needed more milk than recipe called for to make it fluffy.  Great on top of chocolate brownies and with a chocolate drizzle.

text:
Add another victim to the greasy, blobby result list. I followed the recipe exactly, using all-natural-have-to-stir-in-the-oil PB and 2% milk. I also live in Honolulu with no air conditioning, which I suspect may have something to do with my results. Heat and humidity seem to mess with a lot of the things I try to make, often in unexpected ways -- problems I never had before I transplanted myself from the northern Midwest. I haven't seen any of the others with poor results comment on their climate or kitchen conditions (or any of the successful bakers either, for that matter) but I wonder if this explains the dichotomy in the results.  In the end, I mixed in some supermarket brand "peanut butter spread" (i.e. peanut butter with added sugar, oil, and stabilizers) and it kind came together enough to use -- but was neither fluffy nor spreadable, just a thick paste that oozed across the top of the cake.

text:
It took me three tries to make this work. I think the first two failures were due to not creaming the butter and PB properly and perhaps by using reduced fat PB. For my successful try I used the modifications suggested by Cyndie Scheider. Her changes were to use 1-1/4 cup PB, 1-1/2 cup powdered sugar and 3 tablespoons of cream. I creamed the butter and PB with my old Sunbeam Mixmaster on speed 7 for probably 3 minutes. I slowed down the mixer considerably to add the powdered sugar. I added the cream as she suggested and whipped it for 3-4 minutes on speed 11. Tastes good and spreads easily.

I always read the reviews before I make any recipe, so I'm here to assure you that this recipe is full proof. No fuss. No recipe changes. Just ridiculously delicious. Make sure your butter is softened and your peanut butter in relatively fresh (no oil separation in the jar) and your frosting will be flawless. I took a few extra minutes whipping my butter and peanut butter together before adding my powdered sugar to insure fluffiness. I will make is again in a heartbeat!

text:
I have made this recipe for years... at least since 2010. It is my go-to frosting recipe! I finally made a username for this site so I could write a review. 
Helpful hints: 
-make sure to use butter, NOT margarine. Margarine is probably the reason why a few say it's greasy. 
-Make sure to use POWDERED sugar, not regular. Sometimes frosting recipes can use either, this is NOT one of those recipes. -If you have a stand mixer (such as a kitchenaid), it will work MUCH better for a smooth, creamy frosting. When I tried it with my handmixer, it was much thicker and very hard to spread.

 I hope this helps!

text:
This really is a very good recipe but after reading reviews it seems many were either giving it 5 stars or just 1 star.  I felt maybe I could offer some tips to help those who want to try it. It does come out very light and fluffy! 

 Tip #1 would be to make sure you use butter only and your butter is very, very soft. (like it sat out on the counter all day kind of soft).  I zapped mine in the microwave at 3rd power for 90 seconds,  the bottom was starting to melt. 

Tip #2 make sure you mix the butter and peanut butter enough.  After it's mixed keep beating for a couple of extra minutes so they are completely blended together. 

 Tip #3  I was short on powdered sugar so I only was able to about 1 cup. Add a small amount at a time and keep mixing! Again you really need everything to be very well mixed together for it to get smooth and fluffy.

 I did add 2 teaspoons of milk, one at a time, until I liked the fluffy smoothness.  I still have a lot of icing left over after putting it on a pan of brownies.

I feel like mine came out exactly how I wanted to but I didn't use as much powdered sugar as called for.  If I had added the second cup of powdered sugar I probably would have had to add more milk.  But with recipes with just a few ingredients like this one its easy to take it 1 step at a time and adjust for your own personal taste.
 
I think the most important things to remember are to use only really butter that is super softened and be sure to spend the  extra minutes with

text:
Absolutely delicious!! It's a new staple in this house. I made this to top chocolate cupcakes and sprinkled it with chocolate shavings. Everyone who had one raved about the frosting! Im making a batch in just a few minutes for a cupcake order for tomorrow!
One pointer: don't add any milk until you've mixed the other ingredients for a little bit. I didn't wait very long after I started mixing. The mixture looked dry and clumpy so I added a tiny bit of milk. Turns out it didn't need it. The next batch, I mixed it longer and the mixture went from a dry clump that looked like a ball of cookie dough to a delightfully fluffy yet firm frosting. No milk needed! It piped on smoothly and held its shake nicely. Truly a perfect frosting to decorate with!

I've tried doing this before without a recipe and it came out grainy. This recipe was very similar to my previous attempt so the question is why did it work this time and not before. text:
I read some reviews about people complaining and I just don't see why! I creamed the butter and the creamy peanut butter together until it reached a gorgeous creamy texture. Then, I added just under a cup of icing sugar (halved the recipe) and whipped it up until the lumps were out. It was thick at this point, but if you patiently add milk 1/2 tablespoon at a time, scraping down the sides and mixing as you go along, you should reach your desired consistency without any problem. I found it held up the piped design very well and tasted great at room temperature and fresh from the fridge. It was like eating a cloud of peanut buttery goodness and this coming from someone who's not the biggest fan of peanut butter! I highly suggest following the recipe as is without trying to substitute the ingredients or switching the method. Loved it!

text:
Wonderfully light and fluffy texture.  Perfect amount of "peanut-buttery" taste in the flavor that is very different than any peanut butter icings I've ever tasted.  Very easy to make.  Ready to spread as soon as you mix it.  Because of that fluffy texture, it performed MUCH better coming from an icing bag than when I tried to spread it.  You CAN spread it but have to purposefully lean toward creating lots of peaks, because you cannot get a smooth surface at all.

Made this for a Chocolate Wacky Cake as a quick dessert, and it came out perfect once I made a couple of changes: 1. text:
Wonderful recipe. If you do not have an electric mixer you can heat the peanut butter and butter to melting, mix in the powdered sugar and milk, and leave it to stiffen. It will stiffen in about 5 minutes at room temperature. Doing it this way makes the powder sugar much easier to mix in, and I mixed this frosting by hand.

text:
I am not a big fan of peanut butter but wanted to try this since I had all the ingredients on hand. Using some of the suggestions I found on here, I reduced the sugar to 1 1/2 cups, made sure everything including the heavy cream I used was at room temp, added the sugar 1/2 cup at a time followed by a tablespoon of cream, and I also added some vanilla. I beat it for 3 minutes or so and ended up with a wonderful, creamy textured frosting. It was more than enough to cover my 9by12 chocolate cake. It did not come out greasy or too sweet. I think next time I will make a devil's food layer cake and after frosting will pat chocolate sprinkles on the side. Thank you for the recipe.

My 5-star rating is based on taste.

I followed the recipe exact and absolutely love the rich peanut buttery taste that this recipe lends. I made cupcakes from the Black Magic recipe (here on this site) and wanted to try it with a variety of frostings, Peanut Butter at the top of that list. Since I only made 18 cupcakes, I halved the recipe. What I found is that even using the exact ingredient proportions left the frosting: 1) a bit dry after it sat as it appeared to thicken, which was great; and 2) extremely too thick to pipe (using tip 21). I will definitely be keeping this recipe and will modify the liquid as needed to accommodate my treat (cake, brownies, etc.).

text:
I originally made this frosting recipe for the peanut chocolate cake recipe which unfortunately isn't on the site anymore because the one that was with the recipe used way too much confectioners sugar and I only had enough for a smaller amount.  This frosting is light and fluffy and very peanut buttery, perfect for the peanut butter addict like me.  I didn't need all the milk the first go, but the second time round I did, mainly due to the fact that I used a different drier brand of peanut butter.  I also couldn't resist slipping in a little vanilla (or homemade vanilla paste which is my favourite flavour right now) which just perked it up a little as vanilla often does.

text:
I have tried several peanut butter frostings, and this one takes the cake. ;) (pun intended!). I followed the recipe as stated except for blending each ingredient after adding:   I added 1/2 c of butter, 1 cup peanut butter and creamed well, for about 3 minutes. Then, I added 1 cup of confectionary sugar and blended well.  Added the other cup and also blended well.  I then eyeballed about 3-4Tbs of milk (didn't have cream on hand) and mixed well.  I wanted a slightly thick frosting though.  I have already put this recipe in my box.  I love it.  Absolutely perfect!

text:
I made this recipe to top homemade banana chocolate chip cupcakes. The frosting turned out perfectly. I followed the recipe exactly as it's written. I used the whisk attachment for my kitchen aid stand mixer. I made sure the butter was softened. I whipped the pb and butter for about 5 min, scraping down the bowl occasionally. I gradually added the powdered sugar and scraped down the bowl occasionally. I beat it on high speed for about 5 minutes and then added 1tbs of skim milk at a time, using 3 total. I continued to beat on high for a few more minutes. It's fluffy and perfect. Makes enough for about 24 cupcakes.

After reading other reviews, I was careful adding the confectioner's sugar. I found that at 1.5 cups, it was way too dry. So, I didn't add any more, and added the milk as directed. It was very good. I live in a very dry climate, maybe in a more humid climate the extra 1/2 cup is necessary?  I would suggest you add the confectioner's sugar a little at a time, and stop when the consistency is correct.

text:
This recipe is AMAZING!!! I altered it a little because I don't like using milk in my frostings. So here's what I did: Mix butter and peanut butter until you cannot see butter anymore ad the mixture is very creamy (at least 1 min). Add icing sugar and mix for about 30 sec then add 1 tbsp of water. Mix on Med-High (6 on mKitchen-Aid) for at least 3 min. Not only is this a very esy recipe but it's so delicious and a perfect compliment to any cake or brownie. For anyone having trouble with the consistency my advice would be to mix more, 3 min is longer than it seemes. Enjoy!!!

I had great luck with this recipe. It did beat up fluffy and I did pipe it on my cupcakes and it held its shape well. I added about 1/2 a cup more sugar and I just eyeball the milk when I added it but the measurements seem right. Just because it is butter and peanut butter, it might not hold up well in heat, like a summer picnic but we had NO PROBLEM. From experience, I know the key to fluffy is room temperature ingredients as well a beating in the air with every step...first with the creaming of the wet and then as the sugar is added and then as you add the milk. Great peanut butter flavor!

text:
GREAT recipe!!! I used the regular Jiff Peanut Butter, Organic Fat Free Milk, Giant Eagle Butter with salt and Giant Eagle Powdered Sugar. 

I left my butter on the oven while I baked my cakes. It was sift almost to melting point when I used it. I blended the peanut butter and regular butter until well blended. I added 1/4 cup of confectioners sugar until well blended. I added 1 Tbsp of milk at these intervals. After 3/4 c, 1 1/2 c and 2 cups of confectioners sugar has been added. I used my Kitchen Aide Mixer and beat it at medium speed for 1 minute. It was the right texture! I used it in the middle layer of a round chocolate cake!. used whipped chocolate frosting and decorated the top with mini reese's cups and the sided with the tiniest toll house chocolate morsels!!!!

The cake came out great! This filling was just what I was looking for!! THANK YOU! :)

text:
Holy fluffiness!!!  This frosting is a-m-a-z-i-n-g!  Mine was not at all greasy, and it was SUPER fluffy!  A tad hard to spread, but let's face it, anything with peanut butter is not going to be the easiest thing to work with ;)  I softened my butter in the microwave, added the peanut butter, and used a cheap hand mixer to blend it completely together.  Then added 1/2 cup of powdered sugar at a time - with a tiny splash of milk each time as well.  Probably used a little under 2 cups of powdered sugar.  AWESOME recipe!!!

city:

None
country:
None
text:
This frosting was very yummy and indeed came out light and fluffy as promised. It had a great peanut butter flavor. I would've given it 5 stars but I found it to be a tad bit too sweet. I think next time I will add just a bit less sugar and that should fix it up. This frosting was very easy to spread. For those of you who are having trouble getting it to be spreadable, you really need to make sure that everything is room temperature and that it is well combined. Also, make sure that you are adding the sugar a little at a time. You may not be adding enough milk. Remember, the recipe says 3 tbsp or AS NEEDED. Mine indeed take more than 3 tbsp. If it is not light and fluffy then you need to mix it longer. This recipe was great to do in the KitchenAid. Thanks for the recipe. It will be going into my recipe box for sure.

text:
This frosting is very easy and delicious.  I used heavy cream instead of milk, just because I had some I needed to use up.  I didn't measure the cream, I just poured it in little by little until the frosting was nice and light.  As another reviewer pointed out, the butter should be softened, not just at room temperature and it comes out great and spread easily.  It's thicker than buttercream, but very easy to spread if you've made it by the directions.  My kids and husband just got to lick the leftovers off the beater and loved it too.  Great recipe as is...no need to make changes.

text:
I have made this recipe twice now with somewhat better results the second time around. Both times I used it to frost a banana cake. I had two exceptions with this recipe. The first being that the frosting was too thin with the ingredient amounts as written. The second was that the frosting separated slightly showing a glisten of oil(from either the butter or the natural oil in the peanut butter)on the surface. I solved the first problem by cutting back on the butter to 3/4 of a stick of butter and increasing the confectioner's sugar to around 4-5 cups. The only way I could figure out how to fix the oil problem was to keep the frosting and whatever it was frosting refrigerated. Had it not been for these two small problems I would have given this one 5 stars.

photo:
https://images.media-allrecipes.com/userphotos/50x50/5674169.jpg
city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
My mom has made this frosting for years to top a store bought spice cake mix.  It helps to change the order in which you add the ingredients and to use everything at room temperature - cream the butter with a spoon, mix in the conf. sugar (the butter and sugar don't meld at this point so you will still see little flecks of yellow), add milk a little at a time, mixing WELL after each addition. If you don't stir well, you'll end up adding too much milk. If you do add too much, slowly add a little more confectionery sugar.  Once the frosting is smooth, I add one tablespoon at a time of PB until it reaches the right flavor.  I do not use an electric mixer and I use stick margarine, not butter.  I only use Jif creamy Peanut Butter. I sometimes had a quick splash of vanilla as well, but it does make it too sweet for some people's tastes.  This basic icing (without the PB) works great with other flavors as well - for Halloween we use orange flavoring and coloring to ice cut out pumpkins!

Very good. I did not have a problem with the frosting being greasy. As for substitutions, I softened both the peanut butter and butter and the butter in the microwave before mixing. This eliminated the need for any milk. I also used just a little more peanut butter than the recipe calls for and sifted through the confectioners sugar while adding it to make the frosting extra smooth. I served it on top of mini brownies and it was a hit! Will definitely use again!

text:
If you like peanut butter, this frosting is for you!  It was absolutley delicious.  I put it on a chocolate cake made from a box mix and it transformed the cake into a chocolate, peanut butter masterpiece.  I read many of the reviews which made me a little paranoid that I was getting myself into something too complicated, but I followed the recipe exactly, except I might have added a tiny bit more milk.  (I just added milk until it was the consistency that I desired.)  I would agree with all of the other readers- the key is to make sure the butter is room temperature.  If it is, it just blends right in beautifully with the peanut butter. I have no idea why some people thought it was greasy.  Perhaps as one reader suggested, maybe they used bargain peanut butter? I used Skippy and I see other readers used Jif with no problem.  This recipe was fast and easy to make.  I will never put ready-made frosting on a chocolate cake ever again!

text:
I followed the recipe exactly and I think it tastes absolutely great!  The only thing I didn't like about the recipe is the consistency after I beat the frosting.  I had the perfect spreading consistency and was extremely pleased with everything up until the very end when the recipe calls to beat the frosting for at least 3 minutes.  I didn't even beat it for 2 minutes because the frosting started getting very thick and "cookie dough-like".  I even tried adding more milk which helped a little, but I would recommend not beating the frosting at the end, unless you want a harder more dough-like frosting.

text:
Great frosting! I love how this frosting is not too sweet or overpowering. I used natural peanut butter because I find the regular kind too heavy and sugary. Skippy makes a nice natural peanut butter that doesn't require stirring and doesn't have that layer of oil sitting on top. The traditional natural peanut butter probably wouldn't have worked well with this recipe.  But the Skippy was great! I also made sure to allow the Kitchen Aide mixer to do its thing for about 5 mins. I stopped it periodically to scrape down the sides of the bowl and to note the texture. If it was too grainy I added a splash of non-dairy creamer (allergic to milk protein)and let it continue to mix. Don't cut the mix-time short because you'll end up with heavy unspreadable frosting. Mine turned out fluffy, easy to spread and there was plenty for a double layer nine-inch cake. I used a German Chocolate box mix..great combo. Also tried it with a blob of cool whip on top...awesome! I can't wait to try it on brownies!

text:
Decent recipe, husband liked it, but I wouldn't exactly describe it as "fluffy". I used Smucker's 'natural' peanut butter and it was a little gritty and the oil separated. I recommend using the regular! Make sure the butter is softened (the stick will bend slightly) and add milk AS NEEDED... I ended up using almost a half a cup of milk. I used this on a chocolate cake, melted chocolate chips and smoothed a layer on top of that. DELICIOUS! Like a peanut butter cup...
